{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-19 20:37:44","updatedTime":"2020-08-19 20:37:44","title":"Dual-SIM phones are amazing, but in the U.S., carriers hate them","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/androidcentral/~3/FArjFMMNfOo/why-dont-we-see-very-many-dual-sim-phones-us","description":"<div class=\"field field-name-body field-type-text-with-summary field-label-hidden\"><div class=\"field-items\"><div class=\"field-item even\"><p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/why-dont-we-see-very-many-dual-sim-phones-us\" title=\"Dual-SIM phones are amazing, but in the U.S., carriers hate them\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2016/08/honor-8-dual-sim.jpg\"></a></p>\n\n<p class=\"intro\">Some of us need them, many of us want them, but few are offered.</p>\n\n<p>A <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/best-dual-sim-android-phone\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">dual-SIM phone</a> — one where you have two different lines of service available (almost) at once — can be a very useful thing. It allows you to have a business number and a personal number on the same device and you can use two carriers to make sure you always have coverage. They're a common thing in many parts of the world, but rare for phones marketed to the United States.</p>\n\n<p>You might think that these reasons sound great and are wondering why you can't just head to the <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/t-mobile-reaches-major-merger-milestone-officially-retires-sprint-brand\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">T-Mobile store</a> and grab a new <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/samsung-galaxy-note-20\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Galaxy Note 20</a> that's dual-SIM capable. You're not alone. It all boils down to two things — an actual need and the fact that U.S. carriers don't like the idea.</p>\n\n<h2>The U.S. mobile market is different</h2>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/why-dont-we-see-very-many-dual-sim-phones-us\" title=\"Dual-SIM phones are amazing, but in the U.S., carriers hate them\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2019/12/verizon-coverage-map.jpg\"></a></p>\n\n<p>In the States, there are <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/t-mobile-sprint-faq\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">three nationwide carriers</a> as well as many smaller regional carriers that mostly piggy-back on them. These are fully private (and largely unregulated when it comes to business practices) companies even though they often receive federal funding for expansion and maintenance costs.</p>\n\n<p>The actual geography of the U.S. is different, too. Here in the U.S., you'll find huge areas of little or no population but these places still have service for the most part. We've all been to dead spots, but you can usually get a signal from at least one carrier everywhere you'll ever go. Carriers use this as a reason to charge so much more than the rest of the world when it comes to a cell phone plan, and we can't say they're wrong — maintaining a network where nobody lives to use it and pay for it means the rest of the country gets to pay more.</p>\n\n<blockquote class=\"pull left\">\n  <p>The U.S. is different (and weird) when it comes to the mobile market.</p>\n</blockquote>\n\n<p>Many parts of the world aren't like this. Throughout Africa, Asia, Europe, and South America you'll find things like small regional independent carriers, places where they are no coverage and no plans to expand to include it, and highly regulated government-backed companies that provide cell service.</p>\n\n<p>This helps keeps costs lower and makes a dual-SIM phone something many people actually need. You can drive or take a train for just a few hours and end up somewhere that you would be roaming or even a place where your service <em>can't</em> work because it's government-sponsored for a specific region. You'll also need a satellite phone for many places, which is something we don't have to worry about.</p>\n\n<p>This will be a very unpopular opinion, but because the U.S. has nationwide coverage from most carriers and because service is so expensive, we don't <em>need</em> dual-SIM phones. I've used one and they can be really handy, but options like <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-voice-excellent-features-finally-work-google-fi\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Google Voice</a> can do the same thing. This opinion would be different if roaming was still a big thing or if the government decided Verizon could only work in a few specific states. We might want to see dual-SIM phones in those cases, but we don't really need them unless we do a lot of international travel or live close to the border with Canada or Mexico.</p>\n\n<h2>Your phone was built for a carrier</h2>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/why-dont-we-see-very-many-dual-sim-phones-us\" title=\"Dual-SIM phones are amazing, but in the U.S., carriers hate them\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/04/t-mobile-ceo-mike-sievert.jpg\"></a></p>\n\n<p>Another thing that's common in the U.S. but not so much in the rest of the world is how we buy our phones — directly from a carrier through a service contract or a financing option.</p>\n\n<blockquote class=\"pull right\">\n  <p>In the U.S., most high-end phones are sold to carriers, not consumers.</p>\n</blockquote>\n\n<p>That means Samsung, for example, makes phones for marketing in the States the way carriers like them to be made because the carriers are its actual customer. Luckily, most of the things the carrier wants to see are the things we like to see: big bright screens, <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/heres-every-us-city-5g-coverage-right-now\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">fast network speeds</a>, and extras like waterproofing or <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/best-wireless-charging-pads\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">wireless charging</a>.</p>\n\n<p>One of the things the carriers <strong>do not</strong> like is dual-SIM capability. When you buy a phone from Verizon or T-Mobile, you pay them for it but they did not get it for free. A carrier makes most of its money by selling you service, so giving you the ability to buy a phone and use another company for cell service cuts into the bottom line.</p>\n\n<blockquote class=\"pull left\">\n  <p>Carriers care more about locking you in that selling you a phone.</p>\n</blockquote>\n\n<p>This is also why carriers used to only sell locked phones and fought so hard against eSIM technology — both make it easy to buy a new phone and use it somewhere else and it means you might not have to buy a new phone if you switch. Carriers love nothing more than keeping a customer locked in year after year and getting that $100 or more you spend every month.</p>\n\n<p>Since most people don't switch carriers, this system works for the most part. Even business travelers will often just buy an international roaming package from their carrier and not care about having a dual-SIM phone unless they visit a place like China where network bands are very different.</p>\n\n<h2>You can find them if you look for them</h2>\n\n<p>Dual-SIM phones are available in the U.S. even if they aren't very well advertised. You'll find them <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/best-unlocked-phone\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">unlocked</a> on places like Amazon or eBay from many different manufacturers. With eSIM technology, where a virtual SIM card can be downloaded from a carrier, phones like the <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-pixel-4-xl-review-6-months\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Google Pixel 4</a> are also dual-SIM capable.</p>\n\n<blockquote class=\"pull right\">\n  <p>You can find dual-SIM phones if you go looking for them.</p>\n</blockquote>\n\n<p>You can also buy a phone directly from its manufacturer and get a dual-SIM model that works with U.S. carriers, though that may mean you're paying full-price all at once. <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/e?link=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.anrdoezrs.net%2Flinks%2F100048248%2Ftype%2Fdlg%2Fsid%2FUUacUdUnU92704YYr%2Fhttps%3A%2F%2Fwww.samsung.com%2Fus%2Fsmartphones%2Fgalaxy-note20-5g%2Fbuy%2F&#38;token=9TpOUuvj\" title=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Samsung</a> and <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/e?link=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.awin1.com%2Fcread.php%3Fawinmid%3D10855%26awinaffid%3D103504%26clickref%3DUUacUdUnU92704YYr%26p%3Dhttps%253A%252F%252Fwww.oneplus.com%252Foneplus-8-pro%253Ffrom%253D8pro&#38;token=1795mAvk\" title=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">OnePlus</a> are great options for this.</p>\n\n<p>Most people in the U.S. don't need a dual-SIM phone, but life is boring if you can only have what you need. If you really do need one, or just want one, you still have options.</p>\n\n<h3 class=\"category reco-block best-award\">Best dual-SIM phone</h3>\n\n<h4 class=\"product\">OnePlus 8 Pro</h4>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/why-dont-we-see-very-many-dual-sim-phones-us\" title=\"Dual-SIM phones are amazing, but in the U.S., carriers hate them\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/04/oneplus-8-pro-black-front-render.png?itok=piMKD2vt\"></a></p>\n\n<p class=\"subtitle\">More expensive, more capable.</p>\n\n<p>The OnePlus 8 Pro is an impressive and well-designed Android smartphone that's also dual-SIM capable. With other specs like an impressive primary camera, waterproofing, and wireless charging, it's a phone you'll love using!</p>\n\n<p class=\"end\"><a expensive</li>\n<li>Exclusive to Verizon in the U.S.</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p class=\"end\">Setting out to craft its highest-end smartphone in years, Motorola created the Edge+. It's designed to compete with the best of what Samsung and Apple have to offer, and it does a darn good job. The Motorola Edge+ has fantastic hardware, a truly stunning display, and all of the high-end specifications you could ask for. Assuming you're OK with the high price and exclusivity to Verizon Wireless, it's 2020's sleeper hit.</p>\n\n<!-- END RECO-BLOCK -->\n\n<!-- BEGIN RECO-BLOCK -->\n\n<h3 class=\"category reco-block\">Premium for less</h3>\n\n<h4 class=\"product\">Motorola Edge</h4>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/motorola-edge-plus-vs-motorola-edge\" title=\"Motorola Edge Plus vs. Motorola Edge: Which should you buy?\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/motorola-edge-render-no-clock-cropped.png\"></a></p>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Motorola-Unlocked-256GB-Camera-Solar/dp/B08B9SGGRS?tag=androidcentralb-20&#38;ascsubtag=UUacUdUnU92674YYr\" title=\"\" class=\"cta shop norewrite\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\">$700 at Amazon</a></p>\n\n<h4 class=\"pros\">Pros</h4>\n\n<ul>\n<li>Curved display is stunning</li>\n<li>AMOLED screen with 90Hz refresh rate</li>\n<li>Excellent performance</li>\n<li>Long-lasting battery</li>\n<li>Unlocked for all carriers</li>\n</ul>\n\n<h4 class=\"cons\">Cons</h4>\n\n<ul>\n<li>Bad cameras</li>\n<li>No wireless charging</li>\n<li>Cheaper build</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p class=\"end\">The goal of the Motorola Edge is simple — offer 80% of the Edge+ experience for hundreds of dollars less and make it unlocked for all U.S. carriers. Using the Motorola Edge is a joy, as it has the exact same display, great performance, and top-notch battery life of the Edge+. You need to put up with some pretty mediocre cameras and no wireless charging in exchange for that lower price, but depending on your budget, it could be the better buy.</p>\n\n<!-- END RECO-BLOCK -->\n\n</div>\n\n<p>Motorola's Edge series of phones marks its return to the flagship space, and with both the Edge and Edge+, the company has crafted two <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/best-android-phones\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">very good Android phones</a>. The Edge+ is the best of the duo, offering the highest-end specs and most premium experience currently offered by Motorola. Compared to the regular Edge, you benefit from a more capable processor, vastly better cameras, and extra goodies like wireless charging and a metal design. You make a few compromises here and there with its less expensive sibling, but the day-to-day experience of using the Edge feels almost as good as the Edge+ while costing considerably less money.</p>\n\n<h2 class=\"separator\">Motorola Edge+ vs. Edge <em>Price and availability</em></h2>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/motorola-edge-plus-vs-motorola-edge\" title=\"Motorola Edge Plus vs. Motorola Edge: Which should you buy?\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/04/motorola-edge-plus-review-11.jpg\"></a></p>\n\n<p>The Motorola Edge+ and Edge have a lot in common, but when it comes to the phones' pricing and availability, this is where we see some of the biggest differences. The Edge+ is the most expensive of the two devices with a retail price of $1,000, whereas the Edge costs considerably less at just $700.</p>\n\n<p>Even more important is <em>how</em> you're able to buy the two phones. The cheaper Motorola Edge is sold as a universally unlocked smartphone, meaning it's compatible with every U.S. carrier. Whether you have AT&#38;T, Sprint/T-Mobile, Verizon, or any smaller wireless provider, the Motorola Edge should work without a hitch.</p>\n\n<p>Comparatively, the Edge+ is a Verizon exclusive in the U.S. and can only be used on the Verizon network. That greatly limits the potential audience for the phone, and at the end of the day, is ultimately one of its biggest weaknesses.</p>\n\n<h2>Motorola Edge+ vs. Edge <em>Where the Edge+ comes out ahead</em></h2>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/motorola-edge-plus-vs-motorola-edge\" title=\"Motorola Edge Plus vs. Motorola Edge: Which should you buy?\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/04/motorola-edge-plus-review-24.jpg\"></a></p>\n\n<p>The high price and limited availability of the <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/motorola-edge-plus-review\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Motorola Edge+</a> is certainly a bummer, but if you're already a Verizon customer and can stomach its cost, there's a <em>lot</em> to like about the phone. It all starts with that display, which is downright stunning. The Edge+ treats you to a 6.7-inch OLED screen with a crisp 2340x1080 resolution, along with a buttery smooth 90Hz refresh rate. This all comes together with the drastically curved edges, which flow over the sides of the phone like a waterfall. This design makes the Edge+ instantly stand out, and when paired with the sturdy metal construction, you end up with one gorgeous-looking phone.</p>\n\n<p>Flipping the Edge+ over and looking at the camera system, you'll find the best set of cameras Motorola has ever put in a phone. The 108MP primary camera is the star of the show, and it's joined by a 16MP ultra-wide/macro camera, 8MP telephoto camera, and a time-of-flight sensor for capturing more data with your images. The Edge+ takes very good photos, and while they might not be as flawless as shots taken with a Pixel 4 or Galaxy S20, it's still a trusty device for preserving memories wherever you go.</p>\n\n<p>Under the hood, the Edge+ continues to impress. It's powered by the flagship Snapdragon 865 processor, a healthy 12GB of RAM, and 256GB of storage for saving all of your digital files. The 5,000 mAh battery allows for great endurance, and thanks to both 18W wired and 15W wireless charging, it's easy to refuel the phone whenever you need to.</p>\n\n<p>All of this is backed up by Motorola's software experience, which is one of the best that Android has to offer. Motorola's take on Android is one of the best that's out there, as it preserves the clean aesthetic of stock Android while adding genuinely helpful features where they matter. The phone is also backed by a promise of at least two major OS updates, which is better than what we usually see from the company.</p>\n\n<table class=\"spec-table\">\n<thead>\n<tr>\n  <th></th>\n <td>188g</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n\n<h2>Motorola Edge+ vs. Edge <em>What the regular Edge does well</em></h2>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/motorola-edge-plus-vs-motorola-edge\" title=\"Motorola Edge Plus vs. Motorola Edge: Which should you buy?\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/07/motorola-edge-review-4.jpeg\"></a></p>\n\n<p>It's no secret that the Edge+ is the better of the two phones, but that's not to say that <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/motorola-edge-review\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">the regular Edge</a> is bad. It looks and feels just like the Edge+ in so many regards, making it a really enticing option if you don't feel like spending $1,000 on your next phone (or if you use a carrier other than Verizon).</p>\n\n<p>Perhaps the most impressive thing about the Motorola Edge is its display. It has the exact same display as then Edge+, curves and all. Motorola didn't compromise the screen panel, resolution, or refresh rate, which is quite a feat considering the Edge's lower price. The internal specs are also very good, with the Edge touting a very fast Snapdragon 765 processor, 6GB of RAM, 256GB of storage, and a generous 4,500 mAh battery.</p>\n\n<p>One of the biggest downsides to the Edge, however, is its camera system. It's possible to take decent photos with the phone, but overall image quality leaves a lot to be desired. Images are often soft, low-light photography is quite weak, and the camera app itself is often slow/unresponsive where the rest of the phone's performance is just fine. It's a serviceable set of cameras if all you're doing is posting super casual photos on Twitter and Instagram, but if you want to do anything beyond that, the Edge+ is the better fit.</p>\n\n<p>There's also a step down on the software side, as Motorola is only promising one major OS update for the Edge. That means once the phone is updated from Android 10 to Android 11, it won't see any further Android versions. Motorola has had a long struggle with offering good software support for its phones, but only getting a single update for a $700 smartphone is pretty ridiculous.</p>\n\n<h2>Motorola Edge+ vs. Edge <em>Two solid choices</em></h2>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/motorola-edge-plus-vs-motorola-edge\" title=\"Motorola Edge Plus vs. Motorola Edge: Which should you buy?\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/07/motorola-edge-review-7.jpeg\"></a></p>\n\n<p>Motorola has been kicking out rock-solid <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/best-cheap-android-phones\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">budget phones</a> for years at this point, and as much as we've enjoyed those, it's exciting to see the company return to making legitimate flagships. There was some hesitation leading up the debut of the Edge series, but Motorola has proven that it still has the chops to compete in this space.</p>\n\n<p>The Edge+ is marred by a fairly high price and its exclusivity to Verizon, but the fact that those are its two biggest issues is impressive. Whether it be the phone's display, specs, software, or design, just about everything with the Edge+ works incredibly well. It's a unique alternative to something like the Galaxy S20, and for a first attempt at returning to high-end devices, we're thrilled with how the Edge+ turned out.</p>\n\n<p>For shoppers that do have an issue with the Edge+'s price and availability, the unlocked and more affordable Edge is a great companion to it. You get a plastic body instead of metal, the cameras aren't as good, and there's no wireless charging, but the rest of the experience is every bit as nice. The Motorola Edge has a gorgeous display, is plenty fast, and has an identical software experience that's a joy to use. There aren't a lot of phones competing in this \"value flagship\" space, but we're thrilled that Motorola decided to throw its hat into the ring.</p>\n\n<!-- BEGIN RECO-BLOCK -->\n\n<h3 class=\"category reco-block\">True flagship</h3>\n\n<h4 class=\"product\">Motorola Edge+</h4>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/motorola-edge-plus-vs-motorola-edge\" title=\"Motorola Edge Plus vs. Motorola Edge: Which should you buy?\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/04/motorola-edge-plus-cropped.png\"></a></p>\n\n<p class=\"subtitle\">The best Moto phone you can buy</p>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/e?link=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.anrdoezrs.net%2Flinks%2F100048248%2Ftype%2Fdlg%2Fsid%2FUUacUdUnU92674YYr%2Fhttps%3A%2F%2Fwww.motorola.com%2Fus%2Fsmartphones-motorola-edge-plus%2Fp&#38;token=S6uteCi9\" title=\"\" class=\"cta shop norewrite\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\">$1,000 at Motorola</a></p>\n\n<p class=\"end\">High price and annoying availability aside, the Motorola Edge+ is a fantastic flagship smartphone that's worth your attention. Whether you're here for the mesmerizing display, powerful specs, or iconic Moto software, just about everything with the Edge+ is done right. Here's to hoping we don't have to put up with annoying carrier deals for the successor.</p>\n\n<!-- END RECO-BLOCK -->\n\n<!-- BEGIN RECO-BLOCK -->\n\n<h3 class=\"category reco-block\">Premium for less</h3>\n\n<h4 class=\"product\">Motorola Edge</h4>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/motorola-edge-plus-vs-motorola-edge\" title=\"Motorola Edge Plus vs. Motorola Edge: Which should you buy?\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/motorola-edge-render-no-clock-cropped.png\"></a></p>\n\n<p class=\"subtitle\">Lots to love for less</p>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Motorola-Unlocked-256GB-Camera-Solar/dp/B08B9SGGRS?tag=androidcentralb-20&#38;ascsubtag=UUacUdUnU92674YYr\" title=\"\" class=\"cta shop norewrite\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\">$700 at Amazon</a>\n<a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/e?link=https%3A%2F%2Fbestbuy.7tiv.net%2Fc%2F221109%2F615614%2F10014%3FsubId1%3DUUacUdUnU92674YYr%26subId2%3Ddac%26u%3Dhttps%253A%252F%252Fwww.bestbuy.com%252Fsite%252Fmotorola-moto-edge-5g-256gb-unlocked-solar-black%252F6417451.p%253FskuId%253D6417451&#38;token=la7jFx8W\" title=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">$500 at Best Buy</a>\n<a href=\"https://www.bhphotovideo.com/c/product/1571280-REG/moto_paj90004us_edge_5g_256gb_smartphone.html/BI/20079/KBID/13844/SID/UUacUdUnU92674YYr\" title=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">$700 at B&#38;H</a></p>\n\n<p class=\"end\">The Motorola Edge introduces a few quirks not found with the Edge+, but if you're looking for a similar experience for less money, the Edge does a great job at finding that middle ground. As long as you're not a shutterbug, the Edge is a solid pick.</p>\n\n<!-- END RECO-BLOCK --></div></div></div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/androidcentral/~4/eimSuTTtGCs\" height=\"1\" <div class=\"field-items\">\n  <div class=\"field-item even\">\n   <p class=\"intro\">POCO once again proves that you don't need to pay over $500 to get top-notch hardware.</p> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img and today in our POCO F2 Pro review, we're exploring another entry that could be one of the best yet. POCO transformed the value segment with the <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f1-review\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">F1</a> back in 2018. The value on offer made it stand out from other value flagships, and the phone itself is <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f1-review-2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">still going strong in 2020</a>. Following its trailblazing debut, POCO was relatively quiet for 18 months, with the only other device coming out of the brand being the <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-x2-review\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">X2</a>. But with that device aimed at the budget segment, it wasn't the value flagship that POCO fans were waiting for.</p> \n   <p>With the POCO F2 Pro, we now have a true successor to the F1. The phone shares the same core tenets — uncompromising hardware and great value — but this time, you also get a gorgeous design, a vivid AMOLED panel, Snapdragon 865 chipset, retractable camera module, and a massive 4700mAh battery with 30W wired charging. The F2 Pro doesn't debut at the insane $300 price point as its predecessor, but at $500, it's still affordable in the context of the value flagships in 2020.</p> \n   <p>Having said that, the POCO F2 Pro is a rebranded version of the Redmi K30 Pro aimed at global markets. POCO's strategy this year is to stand out on the software side of things, so the hardware itself has been co-opted from Redmi. The POCO X2 is a rebrand of the Redmi K30, and the <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-m2-pro-review\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">M2 Pro</a> is the Redmi Note 9 in another guise. However, that doesn't minimize what POCO is trying to achieve here with the F2 Pro, and with the phone now available in select global markets for the equivalent of $500, let's see what it has to offer.</p> \n   <!-- BEGIN RECO-BLOCK --> \n   <h3 class=\"category reco-block recommended-award\">At a glance</h3> \n   <h4 class=\"product\">POCO F2 Pro</h4> \n   <p> <span itemprop=\"reviewRating\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Rating\" class=\"article-rating article-rating--inline app-none\"> <span class=\"article-rating-stars\"> <span class=\"article-rating-star fa fa-customstar\"></span> <span class=\"article-rating-star fa fa-customstar\"></span> <span class=\"article-rating-star fa fa-customstar\"></span> <span class=\"article-rating-star fa fa-customstar\"></span> <span class=\"article-rating-star fa fa-customstar-empty\"></span> </span> \n     <meta itemprop=\"bestRating\" content=\"5.0\"> \n      <meta itemprop=\"worstRating\" content=\"0.0\"> \n       <meta itemprop=\"ratingValue\" content=\"4\"> \n       </meta>\n      </meta>\n     </meta></span> </p> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/poco-f2-pro.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p><strong>Bottom line:</strong> The POCO F2 Pro offers everything you're looking for in a phone. \n    <li><a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/androidcentral/~3/HkyJruJq8QM/poco-f2-pro-review#display\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Display</a></li> \n    <li><a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/androidcentral/~3/HkyJruJq8QM/poco-f2-pro-review#hardware\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Performance</a></li> \n    <li><a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/androidcentral/~3/HkyJruJq8QM/poco-f2-pro-review#battery\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Battery life</a></li> \n    <li><a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/androidcentral/~3/HkyJruJq8QM/poco-f2-pro-review#software\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Software</a></li> \n    <li><a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/androidcentral/~3/HkyJruJq8QM/poco-f2-pro-review#cameras\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Cameras</a></li> \n    <li><a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/androidcentral/~3/HkyJruJq8QM/poco-f2-pro-review#rivals\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Competition</a></li> \n    <li><a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/androidcentral/~3/HkyJruJq8QM/poco-f2-pro-review#verdict\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Should you buy it?</a></li> \n   </ul> \n   <!--sectionbreak--> \n   <h2 id=\"design\">POCO F2 Pro <em>Design</em></h2> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-3.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>The POCO F1 had what can only be called a basic design, but that's not the case with the F2 Pro. The fit and finish that you get here are on par with true flagships, and like most phones in 2020, the F2 Pro has a metal-and-glass design with subtle curves and rounded edges.</p> \n   <blockquote class=\"pull right\"> \n    <p>The POCO F2 Pro has a gorgeous design with a pop-up camera slider and 3.5mm headphone jack.</p> \n   </blockquote> \n   <p>Both the front and rear panes of glass are covered by Gorilla Glass 5, and the back has a frosted glass finish that makes the phone feel premium. The matte texture also makes it easier to hold the phone, and it does a great job hiding fingerprint smudges. The sides at the back curve gently where they meet the mid-frame, leading to a better in-hand feel.</p> \n   <p>The F2 Pro is available in Cyber Gray, Phantom White, Neon Blue, and Electric Purple color options, and the grey model that I'm using has an understated quality to it that works to its advantage. The aluminum mid-frame adds rigidity to the phone, and overall, the F2 Pro feels much more upmarket than its price tag would suggest.</p> \n   <p>The highlight on the design side of things is the lack of a cutout up front, with the F2 Pro featuring a retractable module for the front camera instead. That means you get an all-screen front without any cutouts to mar the experience, allowing the F2 Pro to stand out in this area. The slider itself doesn't take too long to engage, and it has LEDs on either side for better selfies in low-light conditions.</p> \n   <div id=\"Review_BTF_1-wrap-5f3d1c5003248\" class=\"adunit-wrap adunit-purch\"> \n    <div class=\"adunit-wrap-inner\">\n     <div class=\"adunit\" id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1\" data-clone-id=\"\" adonis-marker=\"\"></div>\n    </div> \n   </div> \n   <div class=\"media-gallery-wrap\">\n    <div class=\"media-gallery-flat\">\n     <div data-title=\"POCO F2 Pro review\" data-big=\"/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/xlarge_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-5.jpg\" data-source=\"Apoorva Bhardwaj / Android Central\" class=\"flat-img \" style=\"background-image:url(/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/w800h450crop/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-5.jpg);\"></div>\n     <div data-title=\"POCO F2 Pro review\" data-big=\"/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/xlarge_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-2.jpg\" data-source=\"Apoorva Bhardwaj / Android Central\" class=\"flat-img \" style=\"background-image:url(/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/w800h450crop/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-2.jpg);\"></div>\n     <div data-title=\"POCO F2 Pro review\" data-big=\"/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/xlarge_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-31.jpg\" data-source=\"Apoorva Bhardwaj / Android Central\" class=\"flat-img \" style=\"background-image:url(/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/w800h450crop/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-31.jpg);\"></div>\n    </div> \n    <!--/media-gallery-flat-->\n   </div> \n   <p>Oh, and another standout is the inclusion of the 3.5mm jack. It's located at the top next to the pop-up mechanism and the IR blaster, and it's great to see POCO retaining the feature. The phone has the power and volume buttons on the right, and there's added visual flair with the power button, which is coated red. You'll find the solitary speaker at the bottom to the left of the USB-C charging port, with the SIM card tray sitting to the right.</p> \n   <p>The F2 Pro has a distinctive camera housing at the back, with the four modules arrayed in a circle. The modules themselves don't protrude too much from the chassis of the phone, meaning there's no wobble when you use it on a flat surface.</p> \n   <p>At 219g, the F2 Pro is one of the heaviest phones on the market today. That's in part to the massive 4700mAh battery, and it's safe to assume that the retractable camera housing and the aluminum chassis also contributed to the weight. For what it's worth, the weight is distributed perfectly across the chassis, and you don't notice the heft with a few days of usage.</p> \n   <p>The F2 Pro is one of the best-looking phones you'll find for under $500, and the sturdy build along with the industrial design makes the F2 Pro a standout option.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"display\">POCO F2 Pro <em>Display</em></h2> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-16.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>The F2 Pro has a massive 6.67-inch FHD+ (2400 x 1080) Super AMOLED display, and the highlight here is that there's no notch or cutout to mar the viewing experience. That's a big deal in 2020, and it gives the F2 Pro a distinct edge in this area.</p> \n   <blockquote class=\"pull left\"> \n    <p>There's no 90Hz display here, but the all-screen front delivers an immersive experience.</p> \n   </blockquote> \n   <p>The notable omission with the F2 Pro is the lack of a 90Hz or 120Hz panel, and that is a letdown considering the device's strengths in other areas. The 60Hz panel is missing that level of immediacy that you get with the <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/where-buy-oneplus-8-8-pro\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">OnePlus 8 Pro</a>, and using both phones next to each other, the difference was easily noticeable.</p> \n   <p>But if you're using a regular 60Hz screen and don't care about high refresh rate panels, there is a lot to like here. The screen has HDR10+, and you get vibrant colors with excellent visibility under sunlight. Colors are great out of the box, and you can also customize the color profile to your tastes.</p> \n   <p>You also get a blue light filter and a dedicated reading mode that switches the panel to warmer colors, and the biggest change here is the inclusion of an always-on display. You get to pick from two dozen clock styles and set a schedule for AOD, and the feature is ideal if you want to glance at incoming notifications and the time without having to wake the entire screen.</p> \n   <div id=\"Review_BTF_1-wrap-5f3d1c500325f\" class=\"adunit-wrap adunit-purch\"> \n    <div class=\"adunit-wrap-inner\">\n     <div class=\"adunit\" id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1_clone_5f3d1c500325a\" data-clone-id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1\" adonis-marker=\"\"></div>\n    </div> \n   </div> \n   <p>The lack of a cutout more than justifies the use of a 60Hz panel, and the F2 Pro is a delight to use for gaming and streaming videos. Ultimately, the all-screen design makes the F2 Pro one of the most distinctive phones of 2020. We've seen brands fall back to hole-punch cutouts this year, so it is great to see a device that offers that all-screen experience while still featuring the Snapdragon 865 chipset.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"hardware\">POCO F2 Pro <em>Performance</em></h2> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-9.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>POCO built its entire brand around value, and the F2 Pro continues that heritage. The phone is powered by the Snapdragon 865 chipset, and as a result, it is one of the fastest phones in the market today. With the unlocked global model <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Xiaomi-Poco-F2-Pro-Snapdragon/dp/B088GQ7Y69?tag=androidcentralb-20&amp;ascsubtag=UUacUdUnU91272YYr\" title=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">selling on Amazon for just $425</a>, the F2 Pro is one of the most affordable options if you're looking for a Snapdragon 865-powered phone.</p> \n   <table class=\"spec-table right\"> \n    <thead> \n     <tr> \n      <th>Specs</th> \n      <th>POCO F2 Pro</th> \n     </tr> \n    </thead> \n    <tbody> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Software</td> \n      <td>MIUI 11, Android 10</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Display</td> \n      <td>6.67-inch 60Hz AMOLED</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Chipset</td> \n      <td>2.84GHz Snapdragon 865</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>RAM</td> \n      <td>6GB/8GB</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Storage</td> \n      <td>128GB/256GB</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Rear Camera 1</td> \n      <td>64MP ƒ/1.9 (primary)</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Rear Camera 2</td> \n      <td>13MP ƒ/2.4 (wide-angle)</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Rear Camera 3</td> \n      <td>5MP ƒ/2.2 (macro)</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Rear Camera 4</td> \n      <td>2MP ƒ/2.4 (portrait)</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Front Camera</td> \n      <td>20MP ƒ/2.2</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Connectivity</td> \n      <td>Wi-Fi 6, BT 5.1, NFC</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Battery</td> \n      <td>4700mAh, 30W USB PD</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Security</td> \n      <td>In-screen fingerprint</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Colors</td> \n      <td>Grey, White, Blue</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Dimensions</td> \n      <td>163.3 x 75.4 x 8.9mm</td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td>Weight</td> \n      <td>219g</td> \n     </tr> \n    </tbody> \n   </table> \n   <p>The Snapdragon 865 is a well-known quantity at this point, so I'm not going to spend too much time talking about it. The only thing you need to know is that the F2 Pro is rock-solid in day-to-day use. You won't find any lag or slowdowns, and it handles the most demanding of games with ease.</p> \n   <p>With the screen offering HDR10+, you can stream HDR content from Netflix and other sources, and the all-screen display is particularly well-suited for streaming videos. The only downside here is that the single speaker isn't quite as detailed as a stereo configuration, but you get the option to plug in wired earbuds or stream over Bluetooth.</p> \n   <p>You also get liquid cooling with the F2 Pro, with POCO noting that the phone has one of the biggest vapor chambers of any phone today. It didn't overheat during extended <em>PUBG</em> sessions, and the framerate was consistent throughout.</p> \n   <p>All things considered, there are no issues whatsoever when it comes to performance. The F2 Pro is available in two variants: a base variant with 6GB of LPDDR4X RAM and 128GB of storage, and a model with 8GB of LPDDR5 RAM and 256GB of storage. Both options come with UFS 3.1 storage as standard, and it's great to see POCO offering the latest modules with the phone.</p> \n   <p>There's also Wi-Fi 6 connectivity, along with Bluetooth 5.1 and NFC for Google Pay. You get AptX HD, AAC, and LDAC codecs for high-fidelity streaming over Bluetooth, and the F2 Pro has 5G connectivity over n77 and n78 bands. While 5G bands are limited, the phone has decent 4G connectivity: 1/2/3/4/5/7/8/20/28/38/40/41.</p> \n   <p>The in-screen optical sensor is fast and reliable, and there were no issues in this area. The haptic engine isn't as powerful as the one on the <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/xiaomi-mi-10-review\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Mi 10 series</a>, but it is much better than the motor that was included in the POCO F1.</p> \n   <div id=\"Review_BTF_1-wrap-5f3d1c500326f\" class=\"adunit-wrap adunit-purch\"> \n    <div class=\"adunit-wrap-inner\">\n     <div class=\"adunit\" id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1_clone_5f3d1c500326a\" data-clone-id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1\" adonis-marker=\"\"></div>\n    </div> \n   </div> \n   <p>Overall, the POCO F2 Pro is one of the fastest phones you'll find in the $500 segment. POCO hasn't missed out on any of the core features here, and the value on offer is astounding.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"battery\">POCO F2 Pro <em>Battery life</em></h2> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-25.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>Combine a 60Hz FHD+ display with a massive 4700mAh battery, and you get a phone that delivers outstanding battery life. The F2 Pro easily delivers over a day's worth of use, and it's easy to make the device last two days on a full charge. You'll get anywhere between eight to nine hours of usage spread across the course of a day or two, and it's safe to say that the F2 Pro is the overall leader in this category.</p> \n   <p>There's good news on the charging front as well. The F2 Pro has 30W fast charging over USB Power Deliver 3.0, so you can just plug in any PD charger with the phone. The bundled 33W charger takes just over 65 minutes to fully charge the battery, and if battery life is a key consideration for you, the F2 Pro has everything you're looking for in a phone.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"software\">POCO F2 Pro <em>Software</em></h2> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-23.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>The POCO F2 Pro came with MIUI 11 based on Android 10 out of the box, and it received the update to <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/miui-12-review-features\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">MIUI 12</a> a few days ago. POCO has committed to delivering security updates at least once a quarter, and in general, there are a lot of positive changes with the customized MIUI for POCO user interface that's on offer here.</p> \n   <blockquote class=\"pull right\"> \n    <p>MIUI 12 is a step in the right direction for Xiaomi.</p> \n   </blockquote> \n   <p>POCO introduced an app drawer on its phones two years ago, and the POCO Launcher has been the go-to option for those using Xiaomi and Redmi phones that wanted the feature. With MIUI 12, the same launcher is baked into the interface, so even if you're not using a POCO phone, you now get the app drawer.</p> \n   <p>An app drawer is just one of a dozen key changes in MIUI 12. Xiaomi has overhauled the privacy settings, making it easier for you to see when an app accesses your location or other data, and you can also automatically remove location data from photos. The system animations have been reworked and are smoother, you get navigation gestures based on Android 10, and there's a nifty floating windows feature that is similar to One UI.</p> \n   <p>There's also a Focus Mode — similar to <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/oxygenos-11-best-new-features\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">OxygenOS' Zen Mode</a> — and new optimizations to dark mode, an all-new Mi Share that lets you easily transfer files, and new backgrounds. MIUI 12 is the cleanest and most optimized version of MIUI yet, and having used the skin for over six years (I started out with MIUI 5 on the Nexus 4), I love the changes that Xiaomi introduced here. This is the first time Xiaomi's software is getting design tweaks aimed at a global audience, and it makes MIUI hold its own against its Chinese rivals.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"cameras\">POCO F2 Pro <em>Cameras</em></h2> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-4.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>Xiaomi has focused its attention on delivering great cameras across its portfolio this year, and the <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/xiaomi-mi-10-pro-review\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Mi 10 Pro</a> takes some of the best photos of any device in the market today. With the F2 Pro, Xiaomi is leveraging an existing formula — the phone uses the same 64MP Sony IMX686 primary sensor as the POCO X2, and it's joined by a 13MP wide-angle lens with a 123-degree field-of-view, 5MP macro lens, and 2MP portrait module.</p> \n   <div id=\"Review_BTF_1-wrap-5f3d1c500327d\" class=\"adunit-wrap adunit-purch\"> \n    <div class=\"adunit-wrap-inner\">\n     <div class=\"adunit\" id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1_clone_5f3d1c5003278\" data-clone-id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1\" adonis-marker=\"\"></div>\n    </div> \n   </div> \n   <p>What's particularly interesting is that the POCO F2 Pro can shoot 8K footage at 24 or 30fps, and the latter is something that's unique to Xiaomi phones right now. Even Samsung's <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/samsung-galaxy-note-20-ultra-review\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">$1,300 Galaxy Note 20 Ultra</a> is limited to 8K at 24fps, so if you are interested in trying out 8K video, the F2 Pro is a decent option. For more mainstream video modes, you get 4K at 60fps and slow-motion video that goes up to 960fps at 1080p.</p> \n   <p>The camera interface itself should be immediately familiar if you've used a Xiaomi phone in the past. All the modes and toggles are laid out in an easy-to-use format, and it's one of the better interfaces around.</p> \n   <div class=\"media-gallery-wrap\">\n    <div class=\"media-gallery\"> \n     <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-imaging-2.jpg\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"></a>\n     <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/thumbnail/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-imaging-5.jpg\" /></a> \n     <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-imaging-6.jpg\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"></a>\n     <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/thumbnail/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-imaging-6.jpg\" /></a> \n     <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-imaging-7.jpg\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"></a>\n     <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/thumbnail/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-imaging-7.jpg\" /></a> \n     <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-imaging-8.jpg\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"></a>\n     <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/thumbnail/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-imaging-8.jpg\" /></a>\n    </div> \n    <!--/media-gallery-->\n   </div> \n   <p>The POCO F2 Pro takes detailed shots with great dynamic range and vibrant colors in daylight scenarios. The camera holds up astonishingly well in low-light conditions as well, and while colors hue warmer, details are still preserved and the shots generally look great.</p> \n   <p>The main drawback with the F2 Pro is the auxiliary lenses. Shots from the wide-angle lens look muddy, and there's no detail even in well-lit conditions. The 5MP macro is similarly bad, as is the 2MP portrait lens. You are getting a great 64MP primary camera and a decent enough 20MP front camera, but the rest of the lenses aren't worth the effort.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"rivals\">POCO F2 Pro <em>Competition</em></h2> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/07/oneplus-nord-vs-oneplus-8-3.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>OnePlus dominates the value segment, and the <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/e?link=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.awin1.com%2Fcread.php%3Fawinmid%3D10855%26awinaffid%3D103504%26clickref%3DUUacUdUnU91272YYr%26p%3Dhttp%253A%252F%252Fwww.oneplus.com%252F8&amp;token=y35TkEnV\" title=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">$699 OnePlus 8</a> is the obvious challenger to the POCO F2 Pro. You get the same robust hardware, a 90Hz display, and cleaner software with fast updates. The F2 Pro has an all-screen front, you get a 3.5mm jack and a marginally better camera, and the fact that it's available for less than the OnePlus 8 gives it a serious edge.</p> \n   <p>If you're looking for the best camera in this category, then the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Google-Pixel-4a-Unlocked-Smartphone/dp/B08CFSZLQ4?tag=androidcentralb-20&amp;ascsubtag=UUacUdUnU91272YYr\" title=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">$350 Pixel 4a</a> is an easy recommendation. You get a flagship-class camera and three years of updates, and while the rest of the hardware doesn't quite measure up to the F2 Pro, the Pixel 4a nails the basics.</p> \n   <div id=\"Review_BTF_1-wrap-5f3d1c500328b\" class=\"adunit-wrap adunit-purch\"> \n    <div class=\"adunit-wrap-inner\">\n     <div class=\"adunit\" id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1_clone_5f3d1c5003286\" data-clone-id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1\" adonis-marker=\"\"></div>\n    </div> \n   </div> \n   <p>India is POCO's largest market by some margin, but the F2 Pro isn't launching in the country. The best alternative in this segment is the <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/oneplus-nord\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">OnePlus Nord</a>, which is <a href=\"https://www.amazon.in/b/ref=sxts_spks_0_0_5d6ff594-0699-416f-bd16-ecb3763ee96a?node=21676199031&amp;tag=mbnx00-21&amp;ascsubtag=UUacUdUnU91272YYr\" title=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">available for ₹27,999 ($375)</a> in the country. The Nord may not have the same level of hardware, but it is just as fast in day-to-day use, and it is available officially in India.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"verdict\">POCO F2 Pro <em>Should you buy it?</em></h2> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/08/poco-f2-pro-11.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <h2 class=\"separator\">Who it's for</h2> \n   <ul> \n    <li>Someone looking for the best battery life in this segment</li> \n    <li>Those that want the Snapdragon 865 chipset for $500</li> \n    <li>Anyone that wants an all-screen design not marred by a cutout</li> \n    <li>Someone looking for a decent mid-range camera</li> \n   </ul> \n   <h2 class=\"separator\">Who it isn't for</h2> \n   <ul> \n    <li>If you want a phone with a 90Hz or 120Hz screen</li> \n    <li>If you need wireless charging or water resistance</li> \n   </ul> \n   <p>The POCO F2 Pro costs several hundred dollars more than the F1, but then again, the rest of the industry has seen a similar hike in prices. The <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Samsung-Factory-Unlocked-Smartphone-Long-Lasting/dp/B08BX7N9SK/?tag=androidcentralb-20&amp;ascsubtag=UUacUdUnU91272YYr\" title=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">Note 20 Ultra starts at $1,300</a>, so in that context, the POCO F2 Pro is an absolute steal at under $500.</p> \n   <blockquote class=\"pull left\"> \n    <p>For under $500, the POCO F2 Pro is an absolute steal.</p> \n   </blockquote> \n   <p>The F2 Pro nails the basics: you get a gorgeous metal-and-glass design, and that all-screen display is a standout feature in 2020. The phone is packing the latest internal hardware, decent cameras that hold up well in most scenarios, and a vibrant AMOLED screen that is a delight to use for gaming or streaming videos. And the software itself is decent enough, with POCO adding meaningful features to MIUI 12.</p> \n   <p>But the key highlight is the battery life; with a 4700mAh battery and 30W fast charging, the POCO F2 Pro is a battery life champion. Yes, the phone is missing a few features: there's no high refresh rate panel, you won't find wireless charging or water resistance, and availability is limited to a few markets. But the pros outweigh the cons by a significant margin, and when you factor in the value you're getting here, the POCO F2 Pro is one of the best phones of 2020.</p> \n   <p> </p>\n   <div itemprop=\"reviewRating\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Rating\" class=\"article-rating article-rating--full app-none\"> \n    <span class=\"article-rating-score\">4</span> \n    <span class=\"article-rating-outof\">out of 5</span> \n    <span class=\"article-rating-stars\"> <span class=\"article-rating-star fa fa-customstar\"></span> <span class=\"article-rating-star fa fa-customstar\"></span> <span class=\"article-rating-star fa fa-customstar\"></span> <span class=\"article-rating-star fa fa-customstar\"></span> <span class=\"article-rating-star fa fa-customstar-empty\"></span> </span> \n    <meta itemprop=\"bestRating\" content=\"5.0\"> \n     <meta itemprop=\"worstRating\" content=\"0.0\"> \n      <meta itemprop=\"ratingValue\" content=\"4\"> \n      </meta>\n     </meta>\n    </meta>\n   </div> \n   <p>The POCO F2 Pro is officially on sale in the UK <a href=\"https://www.amazon.co.uk/Xiaomi-Poco-Dual-256GB-Blue-Blue/dp/B088JWLXB1?tag=androcentr-21&amp;ascsubtag=UUacUdUnU91272YYr\" title=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">for £499 ($655)</a>, but you can pick up the unlocked model on Amazon U.S. <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Xiaomi-Poco-F2-Pro-Snapdragon/dp/B088GQ7Y69?tag=androidcentralb-20&amp;ascsubtag=UUacUdUnU91272YYr\" title=\"\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">for just $425</a>. You miss out on warranty, but for the hardware on offer, it's definitely worth the risk.</p> \n   <!-- BEGIN RECO-BLOCK --> \n   <h3 class=\"category reco-block recommended-award\">All-screen delight</h3> \n   <h4 class=\"product\">POCO F2 Pro</h4> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/poco-f2-pro-review\" title=\"POCO F2 Pro review: The most underrated phone of 2020\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/poco-f2-pro.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Xiaomi-Poco-F2-Pro-Snapdragon/dp/B088GQ7Y69/?tag=androidcentralb-20&amp;ascsubtag=UUacUdUnU91272YYr\" title=\"\" class=\"cta shop norewrite\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\">$425 at Amazon</a> <a href=\"https://www.amazon.co.uk/Xiaomi-Poco-Dual-256GB-Blue-Blue/dp/B088JWLXB1?tag=androcentr-21&amp;ascsubtag=UUacUdUnU91272YYr\" title=\"\" class=\"cta shop norewrite\" rel=\"nofollow\" georiot-ignore=\"true\">£499 at Amazon UK</a></p> \n   <p class=\"subtitle\">A truly outstanding phone</p> \n   <p class=\"end\">The POCO F2 Pro offers everything you're looking for in a phone. It has a gorgeous metal-and-glass design, is powered by the Snapdragon 865, and there's even a pop-up camera slider that leads to an all-screen display. The 4700mAh battery delivers outstanding battery life, you get a 3.5mm jack, and the value on offer here is incredible.</p>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<img class=\"field-items\">\n  <div class=\"field-item even\">\n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animals-hero.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>Google believes in the practical side of augmented reality. For the last couple of years, it's been expanding its collection of 3D animals and objects on mobile devices, from land animals to underwater creatures to birds, house pets, and even dinosaurs. There's also a growing collection focusing on the human anatomy and the internal biology of our organs and cells, along with planets and other objects in our solar system. It's pretty amazing!</p> \n   <p>Unfortunately, Google doesn't make it easy to see every animal or object that you can view in 3D. That's where we come in. We're going to show you every single 3D animal and object Google offers below, along with instructions on how to use them.</p> \n   <!--sectionbreak:article-nav-menu narrow no-amazon mobile-always--> <h2 id=\"howto\">How do you access Google's 3D Animals and Objects?</h2> \n   <p>It's easy to access Google's 3D Animals and other Objects. Just search for a supported animal as you normally would in Google on a mobile device, like a smartphone or tablet (3D Animals won't show up on a desktop or laptop computer). If the animal is a supported one, you'll see a Google Search Knowledge Panel similar to the one that would appear for celebrities and movies.</p> \n   <p>Here's what this process looks like on a step-by-step basis:</p> \n   <ol> \n    <li>Open <strong>Google Search</strong> on your phone.</li> \n    <li>Search for a supported 3D animal/object (we're using \"cat\" for this example).</li> \n    <li><p>Tap the <strong>View in 3D</strong> button.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-1.jpg\" /></a><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-2.jpg\" /></a><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-3.jpg\" /></a></p></li> \n   </ol> \n   <p>This page allows you to view the 3D object with the full ability to resize and move it. If you tap the <strong>View in your space</strong> button, you can even view it right in your home using augmented reality (we'll dive more into that later on).</p> \n   <div id=\"Review_BTF_1-wrap-5f3d1c5007921\" class=\"adunit-wrap adunit-purch\"> \n    <div class=\"adunit-wrap-inner\">\n     <div class=\"adunit\" id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1_clone_5f3d1c5007917\" data-clone-id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1\" adonis-marker=\"\"></div>\n    </div> \n   </div> \n   <h2 id=\"land\">Google Search 3D <em>Land Animals</em></h2> \n   <p>There are a ton of 3D items you can view in Google Search, but for a lot of people, the most fun to use and interact with will be the animals. Whether you want to view something common like a cat or something extravagant like a shark, Google has you covered with a wide array of different animals.</p> \n   <div class=\"grid minimal collection\"> \n    <h4 class=\"product reco-block\">Ball Python</h4> \n    <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-9.jpg\" /></a><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-10.jpg\" /></a><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-11.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>When you first open a 3D Animal/Object, you'll see an animated 3D animal against a white background in Object view. You can slide your finger on the animal to have it move up and down, side to side, and rotate a full 360 degrees so you can analyze every inch, from the backside to the underside. Zoom in by sliding your fingers out and zoom out by pinching them together.</p> \n   <p>You can tap the <strong>share icon</strong> near the bottom-right of your phone to share the 3D object through your preferred app, whether it be Twitter, Instagram, or as a regular text. When you do this, Google generates a link that goes right to the 3D item so people can just tap on it and instantly see said object.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"ar\">How do you use Google's 3D Animals and Objects in AR?</h2> \n   <p><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/article_images/2020/07/google-search-3d-animals-ar-2.gif\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" alt=\"Google Search 3D AR View\" title=\"\" data-source=\"Joe Maring / Android Central\" class=\"image-neutral image-auto fill \" /></p> \n   <p>In the AR view, move your phone around the room to map and process your surroundings. The animal will soon pop up, blended in with your environment. This might take a few tries, so be patient. Once it works, the animal will appear on your floor, perched atop a shelf, on your computer desk, or wherever you want to place it.</p> \n   <ol> \n    <li>When viewing a 3D animal/object in Object view, tap <strong>View in your space</strong>.</li> \n    <li>Tap <strong>Give access</strong>.</li> \n    <li><p>Tap <strong>Allow all the time</strong>.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-3.jpg\" /></a><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-4.jpg\" /></a><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-5.jpg\" /></a></p></li> \n    <li>Tap <strong>Allow</strong>.</li> \n    <li>Your 3D animal/object will appear before your eyes.</li> \n    <li><p>Move around with your phone to look at it from different angles.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-6.jpg\" /></a><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-7.jpg\" /></a><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-8.jpg\" /></a></p></li> \n   </ol> \n   <p>To change the orientation of the animal to see the backside and tail of a cute French bulldog, for example, <strong>hold one finger on the animal/object and rotate it with another</strong>. You don't get the same 360-degree ability to view things like the underside or top of a duck as you would in Object view, but you can turn the animal around so it's facing different directions.</p> \n   <p>If you hold the phone still, the animals will do things on their own, too (like wag a tail, hop, or sniff). The tiger, for example, will open its mouth to roar and the snake will inspect its surroundings.</p> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-12.jpg\" /></a><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-13.jpg\" /></a><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animal-how-to-14.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>In this AR mode, you can also resize an animal/object by <strong>pinching and zooming</strong> on it. It'll be set at 100% by default to give you an idea of what it looks like in real life, but it can be fun to mess with the different sizes. Additionally, if you want to move a 3D animal/object to a different part of the room, <strong>place on finger on the animal and drag it to where you want it</strong>.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"blending\">What is object blending and how do you use it?</h2> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/07/google-search-3d-animals-object-blending.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>Object blending is a feature available on Android devices that allows the animal to better blend into your real world. It allows the 3D objects to sense the world around them and adapt to the room/area they're in accordingly.</p> \n   <p>It's a neat way to make it look like a snake is hiding behind the couch, for example, more realistically displaying only the parts of the reptile that would be visible if it were actually real.</p> \n   <p>It's easy to use object blending. When in AR view, you'll see <strong>a small circle icon on the top- right</strong> with one half that's shaded and one clear. Simply <strong>tap that to turn object blending on and off</strong>. You need to get up close to the animal for it to work properly, and it takes a few seconds for the image to start fading out and blend in nicely. But once it's set perfectly, you can snap a photo to send to friends and family for a good laugh, and kids can have loads of fun playing around with it.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"phones\">What kind of phone do you need to see Google's 3D Animals and Objects?</h2> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2019/10/pixel-4-xl-galaxy-s10-plus-oneplus-7-pro.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>Google's 3D Animals actually work on a wide number of devices, including both Android and iOS smartphones and tablets.</p> \n   <p>For Android, it must be an Android device or tablet <a href=\"https://support.google.com/websearch/answer/9817187?co=GENIE.Platform%3DAndroid&amp;hl=en\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">with Android 7.0 or higher</a> with the Google Play Store pre-installed.</p> \n   <p>For iPhones and iPads, the device <a href=\"https://support.google.com/websearch/answer/9817187?co=GENIE.Platform%3DiOS&amp;hl=en&amp;oco=0\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">needs to be iOS 11.0 or higher</a>.</p> \n   <p>Some of the many devices that Google 3D Animals will work on include the Samsung Galaxy S8, S9, S10, S20, Note 8, 9, and 10; any Google Pixel phone; and select Android devices from LG, Motorola, OnePlus, Huawei, Oppo, Xiaomi, Sony, and others. The iPhone 6S, 7, 8, X, 11, and most iPads will also display Google 3D Animals, provided the iOS is updated. If your device has the Google Play Services for AR app installed, chances are it will support the full Google 3D Animals experience. Google also provides a <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ar/discover/supported-devices\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">full list of supported Android devices</a> and <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/ar/discover/supported-devices#ios\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">iOS devices</a>.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"sound\">Do Google's 3D Animals and Objects have sound?</h2> \n   <p>Google 3D Animals actually do have accompanying sounds, but <a href=\"https://support.google.com/chrome/thread/36849721?hl=en\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\">many users have experienced issues</a> getting the sounds to work on an Apple device. I was not able to hear any sounds using an iPhone XR.</p> \n   <p>However, on an Android device, the sounds are loud and clear. The roar of the tiger is as menacing as if you'd heard one in real life, as is the grumbling of the alligator. The hissing of the Ball python as it moves around gives off the feeling that it's about the strike at any moment.</p> \n   <p>There are some cute ones, too, like the adorable bark and whine of the golden retriever, the nay of the horse, and the quack of the duck. Not all animals include sounds, though. You won't hear anything with the rabbit, for instance, nor the angler fish.</p> \n   <div id=\"Review_BTF_1-wrap-5f3d1c5007946\" class=\"adunit-wrap adunit-purch\"> \n    <div class=\"adunit-wrap-inner\">\n     <div class=\"adunit\" id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1_clone_5f3d1c5007941\" data-clone-id=\"purch_Y_L_0_1\" adonis-marker=\"\"></div>\n    </div> \n   </div> \n   <h2 id=\"list\">What other 3D Animals and Objects does Google Search support?</h2> \n   <p><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/article_images/2020/07/google-search-3d-animals-ar-3.gif\" width=\"600\" height=\"338\" alt=\"Google Search 3D AR View\" title=\"\" data-source=\"Joe Maring / Android Central\" class=\"image-neutral image-auto fill lightbox\" /></p> \n   <p>Google doesn't just offer Animals in its 3D search results; there are tons of other objects and items that you can view in 3D. In some cases, just type in the item and the 3D result will appear as the first one. In others, however, you have to punch in very specific keywords in order to get the right result. \n   <p>Google is always adding more, so keep checking back for updates, or simply Google random objects, animals, and other things to see what pops up in the future.</p> \n   <h2 id=\"summary\" class=\"separator\">Google 3D Animals are fun &amp; educational</h2> \n   <p><a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/google-3d-animals\" title=\"Google 3D animals &amp; AR objects: Every animal, fish, insect, dinosaur &amp; how-to\" georiot-ignore=\"true\" class=\"norewrite\"><img src=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/sites/androidcentral.com/files/styles/large_wm_brw/public/article_images/2020/07/google-3d-animals-hero-2.jpg\" /></a></p> \n   <p>Google 3D animals are a little hidden treasure within Google Search that, once you discover it, is super fun, not to mention educational. It's a great tool for kids, especially, who will enjoy exploring different animals in full 360-degree, 3D views, exploring every inch of their bodies and surfaces. And you can have tons of fun placing the animals into your own environments using the AR View. It's a fun activity in the moment, or even snap photos and send to others to confuse or scare them into thinking there's a snake in your trash can or a raccoon in your garden.</p> \n   <p>As we delve into the other objects that Google offers in 3D, the educational component becomes even more apparent. Students in specific fields can get an up-close look at everything from the planets to the human body that provides far more detail and perspective than a textbook, or even a web page, ever could.</p> \n   <p>We'll be delving deeper into these other objects soon. But for now, have a blast searching for the various animals Google offers in 3D.</p>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/androidcentral/~4/VoNRavfLwog\" height=\"1\"
